The Tiger Knuckle is a punch aimed  at the jinchu, a pressure point     located between the nose and        mouth
This move delivers a downward       rotating blow from the forearm,     aimed at the opponent's collarbone
Unlike the Elbow Slam, this blow    is thrown horizontally in a         sweeping hook
The Elbow Assault targets the       center of the opponent's body       with a full-body rush
A move where the practitioner       momentarily lowers, then raises     their body while swinging to strike the opponent in the jaw
This move involves taking one step  forward with the rear leg and       punching at a mid-level target with the fist
The Rain Thrust is a straight       punch aimed at a pressure point     on the right side of the opponent's neck
The Big Wheel is a powerful         variation of the Elbow Slam.        Aimed at the opponent's             collarbone, it features a diagonal  blow struck once the practitioner   closes in
This move involves advancing a step forward and striking the opponent's chest and jaw with the palm and     entire forearm. The impact creates  a shockwave that affects the        opponent's internal organs
This is a surprise attack with a    spinning backfist. The spinning     motion increases the power          of the blow
This move strikes the pit of the    opponent's stomach with an elbow    bent at an acute angle, similar to  a lance thrust.  Experts can do     this move while spinning, to evade  attacks
The practitioner advances one step  with the forward leg and delivers a slashing blow to the opponent's     side with the side of the palm
A move which utilizes the running   speed of the practitioner to delivera diagonal cutting blow to the area between the shoulder and the nape   of the neck
This double punch begins with a     step forward and a mid-level strike with the leading fist, followed by  a second punch to the same target   with the other hand. Masters of     this move can add an elbow strike
The practitioner firmly places one  palm forward on the enemy's body,   steels and slams the palm of the    free hand into the back of the      other hand in a devastating blow
This advanced move from the Yang    Qing Style involves deflecting the  opponent's attack, and kicking the  opponent's legs at the same time.   It is a closely kept secret, and    not easily mastered
After lowering their body           momentarily, the practitioner then  springs upward to deliver a blow    to the opponent's chin
The practitioner lands a chop to    the opponent's neck using the sides of the open hands. When this        technique is mastered, the          practitioner can repeat the attack  after the initial strike
Iwao Hazuki learned this move in    China. The practitioner strikes a   penetrating blow with the palms     using power from a twist of the     back. Experts can make the blow evenmore powerful by stepping in deeper
The Crescent Kick is unleashed like an upward sword-stroke, aimed at    the opponent's head
This move is similar to a so-called front kick, but is delivered using  the entire underside of the foot    in a stamping action while          targeting the vital organs in the   torso
This is a low, decisive kick aimed  at the outside of the opponent's    knee
In this flying knee move, the       practitioner leaps upward to kick   while restraining the opponent with both hands. Masters of this move    can increase its destructive power
This back roundhouse kick strikes   in a downward motion diagonally     across the opponent's body. The     path of the kick resembles the      surplice worn by Buddhist monks
This kick begins as a high outside  spin kick, but ends as a heel drop. The path of the kick is compact,    and those who master the move       can follow a middle kick with this  technique
This move involves using the power  of the forward leg to deliver a low to mid-level kick to the opponent
This is a high-speed reverse        roundhouse kick. Those who have     not yet mastered the move usually   find themselves off balance when    they miss, but experts can recover  with ease
A kick delivered while flipping     forward in mid-air, this is one of  the more unusual moves in the       Hazuki style. Experts leave no      openings for an attack after the    execution of this move
This flying back roundhouse kick    is powerful, due to the jump and    rotation, but is also easy to dodge.Masters of the move can jump        higher to kick
A flying back kick, this powerful   move aims a diagonally slicing kick at the base of the opponent's neck
This move from the Yang Qing Style  is reminiscent of Taekwondo. The    initial kick is a feint, and after  the opponent is lured in, the       practitioner intercepts with        the heel drop
A daring move which uses the        spinning momentum from the          first spin kick to spin again and   deliver a powerful second kick
Nothing Skill Information
With this move the practitioner     Crouches and spins around rapidly   on the pivot leg while using        the other leg to sweep out the      opponent's legs
With this move, the practitioner    slides toward the opponent, and     kicks upward with the leg, aiming   for the abdomen. Experts can also   aim for the jaw
A simple flying kick, but in the    hands of an expert, a heel drop can be added after landing from the     first kick
While running, the practitioner     suddenly slides forward along the   ground to sweep the feet out from   under the opponent. Experts can     twist to make the attack stronger
With this move, the practitioner    takes the opponent's arm and lowers the body while grabbing the         opponent's collar, lifting the      opponent over the back and throwing
This throw move involves quickly    turning and pulling the opponent's  collar, then using the leg to sweep the opponent's inner thigh upwards  to throw. In Judo, this move is     called |uchimata+
In this so-called sacrifice throw,  similar to the Judo technique of    the same name, in which the         practitioner falls backward to      throw the opponent overhead to the  rear
With this move the practitioner     grabs the opponent's neck and pulls forward and down while reaping the  legs back and up, effectively       applying power in the opposite      directions to the upper and lower   body
The practitioner uses an armlock    to throw the opponent while         flipping forward in mid-air during  the throw to land on top of the     opponent
As the opponent attempts a strike,  the practitioner grasps the arm and executes an armlock to pin.         A common technique in older styles  of jujitsu, execution of this move  varies from style to style
This dynamic move involves          lowering the body to grasp the      opponent's leg, lifting the         opponent onto their shoulders       and then dropping them headfirst    by toppling over sideways
This move involves closing in on    the opponent's side and throwing    down while turning 180 degrees.     This technique is one of the major  Hazuki throws, and dates back to    the early days of the style
Similar to the back drop move used  in pro wrestling, it has been       adapted to make it more difficult   to defend against. The throw is     executed with a twist toward the    rear
This move involving the evasion of  an opponent's attack while moving   behind to attack from the blind     spot
A complex move that damages the     opponent's arms in multiple areas   simultaneously. When executed by    one who has mastered the technique, the opponent is left wondering what happened to them
The practitioner momentarily        crouches to gather strength before  aggressively lunging into the       opponent. Experts can add a         shoulder strike after the initial   impact
This move is an extension of the    Shadow Step. After slipping into    the opponent's blind spot, the      practitioner strikes the back of    the neck
This is a combined defensive        and offensive move where the        practitioner evades an opponent's   attack diagonally, then moves in    for an elbow strike
